Please report on the [blank] day and await reply. He Yingqin bows. (August 21st)"

Hunan Province Merges Eleven Agencies 68

Agency Personnel Stop Receiving Pay, Education Undertakings Virtually Suspended

Changsha Correspondence The public and private losses caused by Peng and Huang's burning and looting in Hunan this time amount to no less than tens of millions of yuan, and it will take more than a short time to restore and compensate for the damage. Currently, the government organs in political aspects have moved to the Autonomy Preparatory Office, the Civil Affairs Office is borrowing the Second Middle School, the Finance Office is borrowing the Second Middle School Attached Elementary School, and the Construction Office is borrowing the Municipal Preparatory Office. The Education Office was initially located at the Second Middle School but moved back to its original office yesterday. All personnel of the above agencies are uniformly only given a monthly food allowance of seven yuan and have stopped receiving pay. The pay will be disbursed after the bandits and communists are suppressed, causing the lives of Hunan's agencies and staff to become more difficult after the great looting. The military organs include the Fourth Route Headquarters, which is borrowing the Youth Association, and the Rural Cleansing Headquarters, which is borrowing the Model Women's Vocational School. In addition, organs such as the Ordnance Depot, the Army Hospital, and the Wounded Soldiers' Rehabilitation Institute have not yet been formally restored. In terms of party affairs organs, the Provincial Party Headquarters is borrowing the Changsha County Middle School, and the Changsha City Party Headquarters has been scattered and has not yet recovered. The Changsha County Party Headquarters has not suffered much loss and is still operating as usual. In terms of education organs, the Provincial Education Association, Sun Yat-sen Hall, Museum, Library, and Popular Education Hall have all been burned down and cannot be restored at present. Although the government has not issued a formal order to suspend schools, judging from the current financial situation in Hunan Province, it will probably not be easy to open them in fact. The only source of funds for the party, government, military, and judicial expenses in Hunan is to rely on the opening of the rice customs. Because Hunan has a bumper harvest this year, it is estimated that at least three million piculs of rice can be released, and each picul can be charged three yuan, which can collect nine million yuan to make up for all expenses. The opening of the customs is scheduled for September 1st. The price of rice per picul in Hunan is currently only six yuan, and adding a donation of three yuan will only reach nine yuan. The price of rice in Hankou is above twelve yuan, so this income is relatively reliable. However, He Jian believes that after such a great robbery, the vitality has been injured, and all non-urgent organs should be abolished to alleviate financial pressure. Yesterday, he specifically ordered the abolition and merger of eleven organs and the statistical surveying and measurement classes (about 880 students) to implement a policy of reducing government. The instruction reads: In order to comply with the order, it is found that Hunan Province has been harassed by bandits and communists, and its vitality has been depleted. The financial difficulties have reached their limit. During this period of suppression, although the administrative construction, local autonomy, and other matters in the whole province are all important plans, it is necessary to consider the facts and temporarily reduce the scope or separately abolish and merge them for selective implementation to maintain the current situation. It has been decided by the committee of this government that the expenses of each agency shall be issued according to the budget of the 18th year, except for those that should be abolished or merged. The salaries of the staff shall be discounted in accordance with other regulations to show thrift. As for the Hunan Local Autonomy Preparatory Office, the Local Autonomy Training Institute, and the two statistical surveying and measurement classes, they shall be temporarily suspended. The local autonomy assistants in each county shall be abolished uniformly. The Sun Yat-sen Library, the Museum, the National Arts Hall, the Reformatory, and the Hunan Budget Committee shall all be abolished together. The Mass Education Committee and the Elementary School Teachers' Qualification Examination Committee shall be merged into the Education Office. The Tung Tree Planting Committee shall be merged into the Construction Office. This is a temporary measure to relieve the financial distress and has to be done. We will discuss the restoration after the financial strength is slightly sufficient. In addition to the separate orders, the heads of the bureaus, offices, halls, and institutes shall immediately comply with the order and report the suspension, completion, merger, transfer, and receipt to be examined for verification. This order. (19th)

Hunan Province Establishes Post-War Rehabilitation Committee 69

Raising Funds for Communist Suppression and Post-War Relief, Accepting People's Petitions for Post-War Issues

Changsha Correspondence: Communist bandits have ravaged Hunan Province for more than three years, initially from Chenzhou and Guilin in southern Hunan to western Jiangxi, then spreading from western Jiangxi to eastern Hunan, and then to western and northern Hunan. Even Changsha, the provincial capital, was occupied by the Peng bandits. The suffering throughout the province has been extremely severe, causing the wealthy to flee the province and the poor to experience even greater unemployment. Providing comfort and post-war rehabilitation is truly imperative. However, at a time of financial scarcity in both the public and private sectors, everything from suppressing the communist bandits and comforting refugees to rescuing the people and stabilizing society requires money. It is necessary to establish a special organization to plan for the most effective way to raise large sums of money and carry out these undertakings. Therefore, on the 18th, He Jian convened a joint meeting of party and government officials and decided to organize the Hunan Post-War Rehabilitation Committee. The committee members appointed include: Wang Qi, Zhang Jiong, and Tan Changkai from the Provincial Steering Committee; Zhang Kailian, Cao Bowen, and Zeng Jiwu, members of the Provincial Government; Wang Jiading, Director of the Fourth Route Army Headquarters Business Office; Fang Kegang, Standing Committee Member of the Provincial Education Association; Cheng Xiwen, Supervisor of the Provincial Relief Committee; Zuo Xueqian, Standing Committee Member of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce; and gentlemen Peng Zhaohuang, Luo Xiankai, Chen Binsheng, Chen Runlin, Xiao Du, Huang Zhenyuan, Wang You, Shi Yi, Huang Yanjun, Su Li, Chen Jieshi, Zhao Heng, and Lei Zhuhuan, a total of twenty-four people. The inaugural meeting was scheduled for the 19th. Separate letters were sent to the Provincial Chamber of Commerce, agricultural, and industrial sectors, requesting each to nominate one person for supplementary appointment, with the aim of achieving the effect of eliminating bandits and pacifying the people within the shortest possible time. The organizational charter of the committee is as follows:

(Article 1) The Hunan Provincial Government has established the Hunan Post-War Rehabilitation Committee to thoroughly suppress the communist bandits, comfort refugees, rescue the people, and stabilize society.

(Article 2) The Hunan Post-War Rehabilitation Committee shall be composed of the following personnel appointed by the Hunan Provincial Government: three members of the Hunan Provincial Party Affairs Steering Committee, three members of the Hunan Provincial Government, one person from the Fourth Route Army Headquarters, one person each from the Hunan Provincial Agricultural, Industrial, Commercial, and Educational Associations, one person from the Hunan Provincial Relief Committee, one person from the Changsha Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and fourteen gentlemen from the province.

(Article 3) The functions and powers of the Hunan Post-War Rehabilitation Committee are as follows: 1. Raise funds for suppressing the communist bandits and for post-war expenses, and supervise their use. 2. Plan and organize local defense schemes. 3. Plan consolation and relief schemes. 4. Make recommendations on administrative matters. 5. Accept petitions from the people within the scope of post-war rehabilitation.

(Article 4) The exercise of the functions and powers of the Hunan Post-War Rehabilitation Committee under the preceding article shall be decided by meetings.

(Article 5) The members of the Hunan Post-War Rehabilitation Committee shall elect five to seven members as standing committee members, and the standing committee members shall elect one person as chairman to handle daily affairs.

(Article 6) The Hunan Post-War Rehabilitation Committee shall hold regular meetings twice a week, and the chairman may convene temporary meetings at any time upon the joint signature of five or more members or when deemed necessary by the standing committee members.

(Article 7) The chairman of the Hunan Post-War Rehabilitation Committee shall preside over the meetings, but if the chairman is unable to attend for any reason, a standing committee member shall be temporarily elected to act as chairman.

(Article 8) All members of the Hunan Post-War Rehabilitation Committee shall serve without pay.

(Article 9) The period for the Hunan Post-War Rehabilitation Committee to handle post-war rehabilitation shall be limited to four months.

(Article 10) For the convenience of handling committee affairs, the Hunan Post-War Rehabilitation Committee shall establish a secretariat, the organizational charter of which shall be separately formulated.

(Article 11) The expenses of the Hunan Post-War Rehabilitation Committee shall be determined by the Hunan Provincial Government and paid from the provincial treasury.

(Article 12) The Hunan Post-War Rehabilitation Committee shall use official letters when communicating with the highest-level party, military, and political organs in Hunan, and shall use official orders when communicating with administrative organs and people's organizations in various counties and cities.

(Article 13) Any matters not covered in this charter may be proposed for amendment by the committee and reported to the Provincial Government for record.

(Article 14) This charter shall be promulgated and implemented by the Hunan Provincial Government. (19th)

Nanchang Bureau of Social Affairs Director Xiong Guohua Executed for Communist Activities 70

Nanchang Correspondence: Xiong Guohua, Director of the Nanchang Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, was arrested by the Garrison Headquarters on the 7th of this month on suspicion of being a communist bandit. At that time, due to the seriousness of the case and the fact that other related criminals were still being investigated, the authorities temporarily kept all information confidential. The bandit has now been thoroughly interrogated, and the evidence is conclusive. He was executed by firing squad at Shagu, outside of Deshengmen at around 8:00 AM on the 20th. Xiong was from Duchang, Jiangxi Province, and graduated from the private Xinyuan Middle School in this province and Sun Yat-sen University in Guangdong. He served as Director of the Political Department of the Fifth Division and Director of the Special Party Headquarters. He was appointed Director of the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs in September of last year. He had shown no signs of wrongdoing since taking office. However, last month, when the Communist Party was approaching Nanchang, the authorities implemented martial law and inspected postal and telecommunications. A piece of mail from Shanghai addressed to Liu Jianshan, delivered by Wang Xiang, a clerk at the Bureau of Social Affairs, was intercepted. The postmark was from a different location. Upon opening it, it was found to be a novel with many illegible characters written in the blank spaces. After careful study by the Garrison Headquarters, it was discovered to be a plan for a communist uprising scheduled for August 20th. The department then detained Wang Xiang and interrogated him at the Garrison Headquarters. Wang confessed that Liu Jianshan was an alias for Xiong Guohua. After obtaining this confession, Commander Zhang sent the Chief of Military Law to the Municipal Government to summon Xiong. Xiong was chatting with Zhang Hongzao, Director of the Public Security Bureau, in his office. When the Chief of Military Law arrived, he presented Xiong with the documents related to the case. Xiong remained silent. Director Zhang then escorted Xiong to the Garrison Headquarters for custody. After several interrogations, Xiong admitted to joining the Communist Party last year with the intention of turning the city's primary schools (which are under the direct jurisdiction of the Bureau of Social Affairs) into a vanguard for communism. He also confirmed that the communist uprising plan scheduled for the 20th of this month was genuine. After obtaining this confession, Commander Zhang, recognizing the gravity of the case, reported it to the Provincial Government and then to the Central Government for instructions. He subsequently received orders to handle the matter strictly in accordance with the law. Commander Zhang, considering that Xiong was using his position as Director of the Bureau of Social Affairs to secretly act as a communist puppet, a crime that was unforgivable, executed him by firing squad on the 20th. At 7:30 AM, the Garrison Headquarters dispatched a battalion of soldiers to escort Xiong along Zhongshan Road and Desheng Road before executing him outside Deshengmen. At the time of his execution, Xiong was wearing a singlet, white cotton pants, and slippers. The white cotton sign inserted on his body read: "Executed: Xiong Guohua, traitorous communist bandit leader, former Director of the Bureau of Social Affairs, for carrying out communist plots and instigating an uprising." A large crowd of onlookers gathered. After the execution, his family hired people to buy a coffin and collect the body. The Garrison Headquarters announced Xiong's crimes in a lengthy proclamation, which is omitted here. On the morning of the 21st, Wang Xiang and three other communist bandits related to the Xiong case were executed at the parade ground, greatly reassuring the public. (21st)

Fujian Provincial Department of Finance Loan Issue Still Unresolved 71

Business Community Appeals for Exemption from Loan

Fuzhou Correspondence: The Department of Finance's temporary loan of 500,000 yuan from the General Chamber of Commerce has not yielded any results as of yesterday's meeting. The Commercial Research Institute convened a meeting of various merchant guilds at 4:00 PM on the 16th to discuss the matter. About a hundred merchants and representatives from various guilds attended. Fang Yingtuan, dispatched by the Department of Finance, first reported to the merchants that Director He of the Department of Finance, facing financial difficulties during this lean season, had no choice but to seek a loan from the various merchant guilds, offering tea tax and bamboo and timber tax as collateral, and issuing treasury bills to offset the two types of tax payments. He had already reported this at the General Chamber of Commerce yesterday. However, Director He was well aware of the current economic decline. If the full amount of 500,000 yuan was difficult to raise, Director He suggested reducing it to 300,000 yuan, with the tea, timber, and money guilds each contributing 80,000 yuan, and the remaining guilds contributing 60,000 yuan collectively, which would be easier to achieve. After the report, he withdrew to rest at the General Chamber of Commerce, awaiting the results of the meeting to report back. The institute then convened the meeting. Everyone agreed that in the past, when government offices sought loans or donations, merchants had always endured the pain and contributed, as they still had some surplus capacity. However, the city's economy is currently in extreme decline. In addition, the ongoing war has disrupted river transportation, causing delays in the settlement of drafts and suspensions of payment deadlines. Bankruptcies have occurred one after another, amounting to several million yuan, a situation not seen in decades. The economy has been severely damaged and cannot be restored to its original state in the short term. Yet, the Department of Finance is still demanding loans, which is truly beyond the merchants' capabilities. Furthermore, loans must be assessed based on one's ability to repay. Currently, merchants are borrowing from all sources to save themselves from ruin, and even then, they are often unsuccessful. To comply with the authorities' wishes, they would have no choice but to sell their wives and children, which the authorities would surely not condone. As a result of the discussion, it was concluded that there was no room for negotiation on this loan. This situation was reported truthfully to Commissioner Fang Yingtuan of the Department of Finance, and the Chamber of Commerce was requested to earnestly implore the Department of Finance to understand the merchants' difficulties and exempt them from the loan. It is still unknown whether the Department of Finance will agree. (19th)

Dispute Over Fujian Province's Supervision of Salt Tax Collection 72

Fuzhou Correspondence: Previously, due to a lack of educational funding in Fujian Province, the provincial government decided to levy an additional salt tax of 50 cents per dan of salt, which would yield 120,000 yuan per month. This amount would be allocated monthly by the Salt Transport Commissioner's Office to the Educational Funding Management Office for educational expenses. However, after the establishment of the Salt Affairs Inspection Office this year, the salt tax was transferred to the office for collection, resulting in significant arrears and jeopardizing educational funding. Now that the summer vacation has ended, provincial schools are unable to open due to a lack of funding. Therefore, the provincial government dispatched Chen Peikun, a member of the Provincial Government, and He Gonggan, Director of the Department of Finance, as supervisors of the salt surtax. They separated the collection of the principal and surtax on salt. The principal tax would still be collected by the Inspection Office, while the surtax would be collected independently by representatives dispatched by the supervisors and remitted to the Educational Funding Management Office for use. However, the Inspection Office believed that this action hindered its authority and repeatedly protested to the Provincial Government, strongly advocating for the continuation of the original system. It also telegraphed the Ministry of Finance requesting instructions. The Ministry of Finance sent a notice to the Provincial Government to persuade them, but the Provincial Government believed that the matter concerned the future of education in the province and deemed it imperative. Therefore, the collection of the surtax continued. Since the collection began on the 1st of this month, the daily revenue from the surtax has been approximately 3,000 to 4,000 yuan, which has greatly satisfied the education sector. The Inspection Office, unable to prevent the collection with the Ministry's order, stopped the transportation of salt from various coastal fields to show its resistance. As a result, the salt stored in the Fuzhou Nantai Salt Warehouse, which supplies nearby provinces and counties, is becoming increasingly scarce, and prices are rising daily. It also telegraphed the Ministry of Finance again. Yesterday, the Ministry of Finance replied to the Provincial Government, stating that, according to a telegram from the Fujian Salt Affairs Inspection Office, the office has been allocating the collected salt surtax as planned since last year, with no arrears. The provincial government sent police to stop them, claiming they were implementing supervision and disrupting salt affairs, and requesting that it be stopped. Upon investigation, the Fujian Salt Affairs Inspection Office's collection of salt tax, after allocating funds for local garrison expenses and repaying foreign debts, has no surplus to remit to the Ministry. In addition to ordering the Inspection Office to handle the collection of the salt surtax in accordance with the established plan, the supervisory measures should be revoked immediately, and Commissioners He and Chen should be recalled, and the collected principal and surtax should be returned to the Inspection Office for proper management to maintain the salt administration. The Provincial Government has now drafted a reasoned reply to the Ministry's telegram. Regarding the shortage of salt in the Nantai Salt Warehouse, it has ordered the Salt Transport Commissioner's Office and the Special Commissioner's Office to consult and prepare capital to purchase and transport salt to provide supplies. (August 19th)

Guangzhou Abolishes Special Municipality System 74

Municipal Public Security Bureau Transferred to Direct Jurisdiction of Provincial Government

Guangzhou Correspondence: Following the central government's decision to change special municipalities to municipalities, the Guangzhou Special Municipal Government only abolished the term "Special" on the 18th of this month. The new seal was only issued in the middle of this month, so the Special Municipal Government only started using the new seal on the 18th. No reorganization ceremony was held; only the name was changed. Because when it was changed from an ordinary municipality to a special municipality, all the old systems were not changed, this abolition of the special system could save a lot of trouble. However, there is one special feature of this reorganization of the Municipal Government, that is, the Public Security Bureau, which was under the jurisdiction of the Municipal Government, simultaneously separated from the Municipal Government and became the Provincial Public Security Bureau, under the direct jurisdiction of the Provincial Government. In addition, the Public Security Bureau usually handles police affairs, and its funding comes from a 1.5% surcharge on the housing rent in Guangzhou. The monthly income from this housing rent for police expenses is considerable. Now that the Municipal Public Security Bureau has been changed to the Provincial Public Security Bureau, and the Provincial Government has clearly ordered that this housing rent for police expenses will still be handled by the Public Security Bureau, this income has been invisibly transferred to the Provincial Government's authority along with the Public Security Bureau. As a result, the Municipal Government's monthly income has been reduced by a large sum. The above are the biggest changes after the abolition of the Guangzhou Special Municipality. As for the internal organization of the Municipal Government, it remains the same. On the 18th, after the Municipal Government was reorganized, it immediately ordered the various bureaus under its jurisdiction, including the Public Works, Social Affairs, Education, Finance, Land, Health, and Public Utilities Bureaus, and the Secretariat, to start using the new bronze seals and submit the old seals with clipped corners to the Municipal Government for verification and destruction. The bureaus have complied with the order. The report of Mayor Lin Yunhai to the Executive Yuan is attached below: A report for reporting matters: Based on the Executive Yuan's Directive No. 2402, which was based on the National Government Office's letter, which was based on the National Government's order to abolish the designation of Nanjing, Shanghai, Hankou, Beiping, Qingdao, Tianjin, and Guangzhou Special Municipalities as municipalities, all previous appointments of mayors of these special municipalities should be canceled and new appointments should be made in accordance with the newly formulated municipal organization law. The order was forwarded to the Municipal Government for compliance, and based on the National Government's appointment order, Lin Yunhai was appointed as the Mayor of Guangzhou Municipality. Based on this, and based on the Executive Yuan's Directive No. 2560, which was based on the National Government's issuance of a bronze seal with the inscription "Guangzhou Municipal Government" and another bronze seal with the inscription "Mayor of Guangzhou Municipality," and based on the Executive Yuan's Directive No. 226, which was based on the National Government's issuance of seven recast bronze seals for the various bureaus of Guangzhou Municipality, the Municipal Government complied and changed the name of Guangzhou Special Municipality to Guangzhou Municipality on August 18th of this year, and changed the Municipal Government to the Guangzhou Municipal Government. The various bureaus under its jurisdiction also changed to the Guangzhou Municipal Social Affairs, Finance, Public Works, Land, Education, Health, and Public Utilities Bureaus on the same day, and started using the seals on the same day. In addition to reporting to the Guangdong Provincial Government and sending separate letters, this document is hereby submitted to the Executive Yuan for review and forwarding to the National Government for record. It is for public convenience. Respectfully submitted to the Executive Yuan. (August 18th)

Suzhou 75

Nanyang Female Students Released on Bail Successively: Zhong Xiuying and Chen Yanru, two female students from Nanyang University in Shanghai, were secretly reported by the university's secretary-general, Fan Kangyuan, to the police district in charge on suspicion of counter-revolutionary activities. The school took the two female students from the district to the Shanghai District Court and transferred them to the High Court. After investigation by prosecutor Zhong Shangbin, Chen Yanru was released on bail some time ago. Zhong Xiuying was interrogated once again yesterday (23rd) and was allowed to post bail because there was no suspicion of any kind. Zhong Xiuying immediately sought out the Hengshan Hall pharmacy outside Linmen to provide bail and was released.

Reactionary Case of Zhongshan Female Student Scheduled for Trial: Yang Zhongxian, a female student of Zhongshan Physical Education College, was detained by the Public Security Bureau and sent to the High Court on suspicion of reactionary activities. Prosecutor Zhu Jun investigated and filed a public prosecution. The trial has been scheduled for the 29th of this month and will be presided over by Judge Zheng of the Second Criminal Court.

Doctor Prescribes Wrong Gender, Petition Submitted for Ban: Hou Yuran, a traditional Chinese medicine doctor in Qiaosikong Lane, Suzhou, recently prescribed the wrong prescription when treating Yang Yiru's brother in Cuku Lane, resulting in Yang withholding payment three times. Later, when treating the daughter of Hu Juemin in Dongbaihua Lane, he even prescribed the wrong gender. Due to these two incidents, there has been much public discussion. Some people have submitted petitions to the County Party Headquarters and the National Government's Department of Health requesting a ban on Hou's business.

Theft and Sale of Kerosene Case, Ship Rower Arrested: Gu Nailin Shipping Company in Sanzhuli, Wenzhou Road, Xinzhapu, Shanghai, hired boatman Wu Fuyuan last month to transport 600 cases (1,200 kilograms, worth about 5,000 yuan) of Texaco Happiness brand kerosene for sale to Xiefengtai in Suzhou. After arriving in Suzhou, Xu Tianyuan initiated a conspiracy with Zhang Jian Tang and others from the Minsheng Match Factory to steal and sell the kerosene. The Wuxi County Police Team arrested a boatman surnamed Ji and escorted him to Suzhou for interrogation. Zhang, Xu, and the stolen goods were found and escorted to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation and transfer to the court. Boatman Wu Fuyuan fled to Taixian after the incident. Xu Deyi, a detective from the Third District of the Water Public Security Bureau, arrested Wu in the hot market in Taixian. Lin Shaoting, a detective dispatched by the district headquarters, took a document to Taixian to escort him to Suzhou. Wu confessed that he was a 26-year-old from Funing who had been rowing boats in Shanghai. Xu Tianyuan was the mastermind of the case, and Wu himself received a share of 280 yuan. The Third District decided to transfer the case to the District Court for trial on the 25th.

Jinshan 76

Gangster Banditry Sweeps Various Towns: For the past month, the practice of gangsters extorting loans has been rampant in this county. Recently, although several bandits have been captured, several have been killed, and several bandit dens have been burned down in various places after the military police's suppression, the practice of extorting loans has not diminished as a result and continues unabated, showing how rampant their power is. It is said that Tai Bao A Shu secretly went to Shanghai again recently to contact other gangs, and many of them have jointly entered the county in the past few days. They have gathered in Liujia Yanqiao, Zhuajiaowan, Luwan Temple, Xinmiao, and Jiehe, totaling about 800 people. As for guns and ammunition, they have also purchased a lot recently, which were transported by sea. At Ma Shouchang's home north of Liujia Yanqiao, Tai Bao A Shu has extorted loans many times. The other day, he wanted to extort 3,000 yuan, but Shouchang was already penniless and unable to pay. He then increased the amount to 30,000 yuan and threatened him in every way. Shouchang immediately moved his family to avoid them. Recently, his house has been occupied by these people. On the afternoon of the 21st, a small part of the bandits, numbering about 80, armed themselves and paraded with red flags raised high, starting from Liujia Yanqiao to Baziqiao and other places to demonstrate, and instigated local ruffians to spread rumors everywhere, saying that the anti-smuggling team had been bribed by these people and that these people would soon attack certain towns and cities. As a result, people were apprehensive. Unexpectedly, at 10:00 AM on the 22nd, all the guns of the 8th Public Security Sub-bureau in Qianjiawei were looted by the gangsters. (Qianjiawei was originally a place where gangsters often appeared, and the chief of the Public Security Bureau, seeing the weakness of the police force, dealt with them evasively, fortunately preserving his safety, so this time the bandits came to loot weapons was not unexpected.) At that time, the telephone in the telephone bureau was also destroyed. However, merchants were not looted. It is estimated that the number of bandits was over one hundred, all armed with guns. Then they roared away. At 2:00 PM, it was heard that the towns of Langxia and Luxiang were both looted at the same time. From this, it can be seen that the gangsters were divided into several groups.

Another message: The notorious lake bandit leader, Tai Bao A Shu of the Pudong gang, who has been entrenched in the Liujiaqiao town in Jinshan County, where Shanghai, southern Jiangsu, and Zhejiang meet, has been actively expanding his bandit party in the past two or three months and has increased it to as many as eight or nine hundred people. Since the middle of this month, it has been frequently rumored that the bandit leader Tai Bao will lead his troops to loot the town of Xincang in Pinghu County. As a result, the residents near the town were extremely frightened. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the 22nd, the bandit party members indeed gathered in Liujiaqiao and divided into three routes to the northwest: one route to Luxiang Town in Jinshan County, numbering about one hundred and several tens of people, and one route to Langxia Town, not far from Luxiang, also numbering about one hundred and several tens of people, all armed with various military weapons and several machine guns, driving more than ten boats and more than twenty horses, advancing by both water and land; another route of only thirty or more bandits advanced towards Qianjiawei, three miles from Zhangyan, led by Tai Bao himself leading the main force (about two hundred or more people) as support for the three routes. At about 1:00 PM, the three routes arrived at the same time. However, although the towns of Luxiang and Langxia each had a Public Security Branch Bureau, each only had ten or more police officers. Qianjiawei only had a police station with eight police officers stationed there. With a total of only thirty or more guns, the police officers saw that the bandits were powerful and well-equipped and were outnumbered, so they could only stand by and watch. All the guns were looted. Although the police officers of the Luxiang and Langxia bureaus resisted slightly, a sudden clash occurred. As a result, most of the guns were also looted. The bandits searched the residents of the two towns extensively, looting countless weapons and wealth. However, shops and poor residents were not harmed. However, more than ten people were killed or injured during the police-bandit resistance (names have not yet been identified). On the Qianjiawei side, the bandits did not cause any disturbance. By evening, the three routes of bandits had joined together again and advanced towards Zhujing, claiming they would loot Zhujing. When the bandits came, they first cut all the telephone lines, so news was blocked. It is also heard that the bandits all wore gray shirts and trousers, which looked like uniforms, and all their actions seemed organized.

Wuxi 77

Committee Member for Clearing Backlog of Cases Transferred: Tang Yiqin, a member of the county government's Committee for Clearing Backlog of Cases, has recently been transferred by the Suzhou High Court to serve as a candidate judge in the First Branch of the High Court in Qingjiangpu. The vacancy will be filled by Lu [Character illegible] Jie. Mr. Lu arrived in Wuxi from Suzhou yesterday and immediately contacted County Magistrate Pan to discuss everything. It is heard that Mr. Tang will have to go to Qingjiang to assume his new post within a few days.

Pawnshop Embezzlement Causes Huge Debt to Qian Zhuang: Jun Da Pawnshop in Qingyang Town, Jiangyin County, is jointly operated by Sheng Yulin and others from Changzhou. Over the years, Jiang Xiangxian, the pawnshop's accountant, Cao Zhifu, the cashier, and Shen Jinqing, the public relations manager, conspired with internal and external staff to embezzle and misappropriate money from the pawnshop, reaching more than 70,000 yuan. Recently, they even packed up the gold jewelry stored in the jewelry room and transported it out. However, they were discovered by Wang Miancheng of the Xian De Pawnshop in this county and were immediately detained. After the San Yinhao (three silver firms) and San Qianzhuang (three money shops) of this county, namely Bao Kangrun, Yongjirun, Ruichangrun, Rui Yurun, Fuchangcheng, and Yongsheng, were reported, and seeing that the pawnshop was going bankrupt and still owed huge debts, they each sent a representative to Qingyang to negotiate seriously. Unexpectedly, Jiang Xiangxian, Cao Zhifu, and others had already heard the news and fled without a trace. At that time, the Suzhou and Jiangyin silver firms and money shops also sent representatives to Qingyang and held a maintenance meeting at the pawnshop. After discussion, it was resolved that the Suzhou, Wuxi, and Jiangyin silver firms and money shops would organize the Suzhou-Wuxi-Chengjiang Creditors' Group. All the pawnshop's affairs would be temporarily maintained by the group. It is heard that the pawnshop owes a total of 110,850 yuan to the Suzhou, Wuxi, and Chengjiang shops, and owes 54,000 yuan to shareholders in Shanghai. The items currently stored in the pawnshop include 65,000 yuan worth of clothing and 16,000 yuan worth of gold jewelry, and over 14,000 yuan worth of silver jewelry. After offsetting debts with stored items, it is estimated that about half the amount is still owed.

The Private Anti-Smuggling Team Launched a Large-Scale Suppression of Bandits: The Second Team of the Seventh Anti-Smuggling Brigade engaged in a fierce battle with bandits at the Jialingtang Xiadianqiao area on the border of Yu and Xi (Wuxi). The bandits, unable to withstand the pressure, fled towards Yuanshan Dang, detouring to Yangcheng Lake to hide. After receiving a report from Li Chuquan, the leader of the Second Team, Wu Hanzhuang, the Captain of the Seventh Brigade, immediately led his subordinates, Zhao Jingshu, the leader of the First Team, Huang Xizhang, the leader of the Third Team, and all the team members, as well as Wang Wenhai, the No. 7 patrol captain of the Third Team, Dai Shoushan, the deputy captain of the Commercial Patrol Team, Huang Zhenou, and others, along with more than twenty patrol boats, to Dang Kou (location) yesterday to meet with the Second Team to encircle and suppress the bandits in Yuanshan Dang.

Police Brigade Captain Replaced Yesterday: Zhu Zhenguo, the captain of the County Police Brigade, has been repeatedly accused to the provincial government, and the provincial government secretly investigated and found the accusations to be true. The county was ordered to dismiss Zhu and appoint Wang Wei to take over in Wuxi. Captain Wang went straight to the team yesterday morning to take over after being appointed.

Citizens of Xixi sent a telegram to the province to appeal that Sun Zuji, the former magistrate of Wuxi, be approved to resign and that Pan Zhong be appointed to succeed him by the Department of Civil Affairs. Measures to relieve the financial difficulties of various county administrations: During the 294th provincial government meeting, the Department of Civil Affairs proposed measures to relieve the financial difficulties of various county administrations. Item 3 stated that the administrative expenses of all institutions with special funds should be paid from the special funds. After discussion and approval, the Department of Finance issued an order to all counties to implement it. All expenses of the county's construction bureaus, as well as agriculture, forestry, and sericulture fields, will be paid from the construction special funds and agricultural improvement mu (unit of area) levies collected by the respective counties. All subsidies originally provided by the provincial treasury will be suspended.

Reactions to the telephone rate increase: After the telephone bureau issued a circular on the rate increase, users have been quite critical, generally believing that Zhenjiang's telephones are unreliable, the equipment is outdated, and the operators are unqualified. Although the authorities have been repeatedly requested to rectify the situation, no action has been taken so far. Now, a sudden increase of one yuan per month has been scheduled to take effect on September 1, and users are rising up in opposition. Among the users, shops account for the majority, all demanding that the trade associations of various industries send a telegram to the Ministry to temporarily postpone the increase. The Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce also telegraphed the Ministry yesterday, requesting that the rate increase scheduled for September 1 be implemented at a slower pace.

Curbing the high price of rice: The price of rice in various places had previously fallen due to the congestion of imported rice and the expectation of a bumper harvest in various places this year. However, rice merchants in Zhenjiang, regardless of selling at a loss, were unilaterally raising prices due to the high cost of purchasing goods. The county party department believed that the rice merchants' actions were clearly manipulating the people's food supply and decided at the eighteenth executive committee meeting to send a letter to the county government to stop it and to summon the rice merchants for talks.

A barge stole and sold goods: Twenty-six cases of Beiping brand cigarettes, produced by the Shanghai Public Land East Tobacco Company, were loaded by boatman Gu Tianqing from the Zhenjiang transfer station to the Wubei Fuji distribution office. However, when the boat reached Gaoyou, the boatman suddenly had malicious intentions and moored the boat in the center of the lake. Pinghu 84

Wu Chonghui robbed a widow's home: In the Dushan Village Wu Chonghui area, there lived a widow, Jin Wu, whose daughter-in-law was also a widow and whose grandson was only fifteen years old. They were diligent in farming, and their family was gradually becoming well-off. On the night of the nineteenth, dozens of bandits suddenly arrived with handguns, knives, and clubs at Jin Wu's house, smashing the door and entering the room. They ordered accomplices to stand guard outside the door and fire shots as a warning. Neighbors heard the gunshots and were afraid to help. The thieves first entered Wu's bedroom and looted everything. Unable to find any cash, they stripped Wu of her outer clothing and burned her skin with wax candles. Her cries were unbearable to hear. They then went to the bedroom of her daughter-in-law and grandson. Fortunately, the daughter-in-law had escaped through the back door, and the grandson was also curled up in the dark, not revealing his presence. They were not harmed. After looting for two hours, they formed a team, fired shots, and left in a northeast direction.

A child bride fell into the river: Hu Heshang, a farmer from Liangzhuangfang, had a young daughter who was given to Ding Aqi's family in Zhengjingfang as a child bride at the age of nine. She has been working diligently for seven years. The other day, she went to the river to wash her feet late in the evening. At that time, it had rained heavily and the river was swollen. She accidentally lost her footing and fell into the river. By the time neighbors realized what had happened and rushed to rescue her, she had already died.

Local bandits Wang Adi and Wang Xiaodi escorted to He Xin Cang: Two notorious bandits, Wang Adi and Wang Xiaodi, were captured by the seventh company of the second battalion of the provincial security team. Xiaoshan 85

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce is actively established: The Xiaoshan Urban and Township Chamber of Commerce previously received the recommended list of committee members of the various township chambers of commerce from the Provincial Merchant Organization and Unification Committee, in accordance with the methods of recommending members of the various county chambers of commerce, and the Xiaoshan, Linpu and Yiqiao Chambers of Commerce have been issued with seals and will be established immediately. It is reported that the Chambers of Commerce in Wenyan, Guali, and other places are also actively organizing.

Request for the prosecution of unscrupulous merchants exporting rice: Linpu in Xiaoshan has always been an area where rice is gathered. This spring, the price of rice has risen repeatedly, and most rice shops have made money. Recently, new goods have been put on the market, and the price of rice has plummeted. Rice shops have felt a slight loss. Unexpectedly, Han, an unscrupulous merchant from Hangzhou, bought all the large-grain rice and secretly transported it overseas, causing the price of rice to rise by one yuan again on the 19th. It has now been discovered that Han has transported 700,000 shi (unit of dry volume) of rice. Xiaoshan and Linpu account for more than 10,000 shi. Yesterday, the public learned of the inside story and telegraphed the province to strictly prosecute Han, and to detain the rice Han transported to Shanghai and use it for price stabilization.

Prostitutes and opium boats along the river are difficult to eliminate: Prostitutes are rampant along the river in Xiaoshan. It is said that the flower boats in Wenyan and Yiqiao are specially for river travelers and mountain travelers to play, and the private prostitutes in Linpu's flower and opium dens are also places for merchants to entertain themselves. Young people have gone astray and become addicted to bad habits, without knowing it. Now, the provincial and county authorities are strictly prohibiting prostitution, but the long-standing habits in our Xiaoshan remain the same. The various public security branch bureaus have been repeatedly accused by the local people of protecting prostitutes and opium dens. Therefore, there are questions about dispatching police to drive them away, but it is difficult to eliminate them all at once.

Ningbo 86

The entire China Cigarette Factory was burned down: The China Cigarette Factory in Wojiagang, Jiangbei, in this port, which specializes in making various brands of paper cigarettes for customers, was quite developed. Yesterday evening, at about 9:00 p.m., the associate manager was out, and the staff and workers were all chatting and relaxing at the door. No one was taking care of the smoking room, causing the cigarettes to burn and catch fire. By the time they realized it, the entire room was on fire, and people could not get close to it. The fire spread to other rooms, becoming a raging inferno. The Yi Long volunteer fire brigade rushed to the scene after hearing the alarm. The fire was too fierce, and it was difficult to extinguish due to the inconvenience of drawing water. After burning for more than an hour, all the houses were reduced to ashes. The loss was estimated at 30,000 to 40,000 yuan, truly a great calamity.

The Dongchen Security Corps in Xiangshan was disarmed by bandits: There are many wealthy households in Dongchen, Xiangshan (20 miles from the city). To defend against bandits, a security corps was established to guard the area, so they have been safe for many years. On the night of the 14th of this month, thirty to forty bandits suddenly went to Nanbu Village and looted the guns of the anti-smuggling team there. Then, they swarmed to Dongchen and stormed the security corps, confiscating all eight rifles. It is said that after the bandits obtained the weapons, they intended to rob the wealthy households, but the people there sounded the alarm by banging gongs and firing shots, so the bandits fled back to Nanbu by their original route.

Shaoxing 87

Petition to abolish the triangular surcharge: The Shaoxing County Executive Committee believes that the provincial government's decision to levy a three-corner surcharge per tael of grain for land development fees is illegal and harms the people. In recent years, various counties have been plagued by rampant bandits and frequent natural disasters, coupled with heavy public debts and special donations, which have exhausted the people's resources. The current socio-economic situation has reached a dead end and cannot bear any further burden. Moreover, there are too many surcharges levied with the grain tax, almost equal to the regular tax. If a new tax is added, it will inevitably exceed the amount of the regular tax, which violates the central government's orders. It was proposed at the twenty-ninth meeting to petition the Provincial Executive Committee to strictly correct this and allow it to be forwarded to the Central Government for a clear order to abolish it, and to show compassion for the people's difficulties. It was also requested that the party departments of the various counties unanimously advocate to alleviate the people's hardship.

The Public Security Bureau apprehended a thief from Tonglu who fled to Shaoxing: The Shaoxing Public Security Bureau received a request from the Tonglu County Government to assist in apprehending Mo Youfu, Zhao Ziliang, and other thieves who fled to Shaoxing for trial. The bureau dispatched four police officers and two detectives, each armed with guns, to work with the Keqiao police on the 21st to apprehend Zhao Ziliang's father and his wife, as well as Mo Youfu and three others in Panjiawu. Two leather suitcases and dozens of pieces of clothing were also seized. They will be escorted to Tonglu for trial in a few days.

Shangyu 88

Bail for the staff of the military recruitment team: The Songxia Public Security Bureau learned that a military recruitment team was acting arbitrarily within its jurisdiction and had no official documents from the county government to inform them, fearing that there was something else going on. On the afternoon of the 16th, they went to intervene with the county defense team and escorted six staff members to the city on the 17th. The trial judge, Zhu Yao, opened the court for trial. According to their confession, they were sent by the First Branch Office stationed in the city to recruit people. Later, the chief of the office, Ye Chuanyi, sent a letter to confirm this, but the letter stated that they were ordered to recruit soldiers and were being unreasonably suppressed, and requested to be sent to the province for handling. Zhu ruled that since the office had not consulted with the county in advance and had arbitrarily carried out recruitment everywhere, it was not only disrupting the administrative system but also hindering local security. He ordered the staff members to sign and wait to be sent to the province for handling. The chief of the office has now personally gone to the government to provide bail.

Anqing 89

The Anqing Branch of the Chinese Engineering Society was established: The Chinese Engineering Society has been established for twelve years, and branches have been established in fourteen places. Its purpose is to unite local engineers, study and apply academics, develop the society's affairs, and the engineering industry in China. The members are all outstanding figures in the scientific community. It is now heard that more than a dozen members have organized the Anqing Branch. Foreign Merchants Mixing in Chinese Manufacturing Markings 92

The Tobacco Exchange Industry Asks to Ban Them; The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Asks for an Investigation

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a document to the Municipal Social Bureau yesterday regarding the protection of domestic cigarettes, stating that it was presenting a case. On the 21st of this month, the Tobacco Exchange Industry Association sent a letter stating that, according to reports from the Nanshi members of the association, there are recently ten-pack Gu Yin brand cigarettes sold by promoters along the street to colleagues. The packaging box shell is printed with the words "Made in China". However, after investigation, Chinese cigarette factories do not produce this brand name. It is obvious that foreign merchants are deliberately confusing the situation, which not only hinders the business of Chinese merchants but also has a huge impact on the future of domestic products. It should be forwarded to the higher authorities for a thorough investigation to benefit the industry and attached a Gu Yin brand box shell. After investigation, Chinese factories do not produce Gu Yin brand cigarettes. How can they be printed with "Made in China" on the box shell without stating the company name and arbitrarily disturbing the truth along the way? It is obvious that they are deliberately impersonating, and the harm to the business of domestic products is not small. A special letter is sent with the original box style to the council, and it is requested that the council approve the transfer to the Trademark Bureau for a thorough investigation to prevent counterfeiting and protect the industry. The dispute in this case is neither a question of whether the trademark itself is registered nor a dispute over which trademark, Gu or Wotun, was used first. It is only because the cigarette box is printed with the four characters "Made in China" that, according to the investigation, Chinese cigarette factories do not produce this product, and the actual name of the company is not stated, which is close to impersonating the name of Chinese merchants. Therefore, it is requested that it be transferred for a thorough investigation. The argument here does not involve the scope of trademark exclusive rights and does not seem to be within the jurisdiction of the Trademark Bureau. The council believes that foreign merchants are using the mentality of Chinese people to promote domestic products, and such promotional texts have long become commonplace. The foreign merchants themselves may defend that the four characters "Made in China" are marking the place of manufacture, not marking the nationality of manufacture. Then, the first thing to be marked in the text should be the name of the company, and the word "in" should be added above the four characters "Made in China" to indicate that they are not shadowing the name of Chinese merchants. Otherwise, the intention is to take advantage of the trick, which is actually harmful to the legitimate rights of ordinary Chinese merchants. It seems that the prohibition should be actively sought to prevent future imitation. It is appropriate to submit the cigarette box to the council for review to determine whether it can be forwarded to the municipal government to prohibit the promotion of this cigarette in the Chinese border and inform the public security bureau to order each district to pay attention to the prohibition at any time to protect the rights and interests of Chinese merchants.

The Fourth District Party Department Opposes the Increase in Water Prices in the Concession 93

The Fourth District Party Department of this city believed that the Public Concession Water Company had another proposal to increase prices, and on the previous day, the Forty-seventh District Executive Committee Meeting decided to issue a declaration opposing it. The original text is recorded as follows: The establishment of the water company was originally to alleviate the shortage of urban water materials and became a kind of common-need enterprise. This kind of enterprise is very different from other enterprises. The water materials are indispensable to every member of the community every day, so the water industry must not be solely for profit under the premise of reasonable remuneration. The establishment of the water company is actually a social public cause and cannot be compared with other enterprises that are for profit. The water price standard of the Public Concession Water Company has increased from 10% to 12%. The burden of water materials on the citizens has increased by 10% out of thin air, which is already unbearable. Now, there is another proposal to increase prices, which is to directly regard water materials as commodities and regard users as customers. The users cannot be without water, and the company uses this to coerce them by repeatedly increasing prices. At a time when prices of various commodities are soaring, the citizens are already feeling overwhelmed by other living expenses, and the water company is arbitrarily increasing water prices, which is tantamount to prohibiting citizens from using water and cutting off the beverage that is commonly needed by the citizens. In recent years, the company's income has increased invisibly due to the increase in housing prices. If the water price is increased again this time, it will inevitably affect the increase in housing prices. Moreover, the company's annual surplus is very large. If it is said that the gold price is affected and the expenses are insufficient, then it can be started from the cost reduction and frugality can be practiced on weekdays. With the company's large income, it can alleviate the temporary tightness. However, the company does not think about the root cause and wants to treat the symptoms by increasing the water prices of the citizens, which is actually placing the citizens in desperation. If the opposition is not raised immediately, the burden on the citizens of the concession will increase and they will suffer a lot of hardship in their lives. The members of this department, in their pain and anger, issued a special declaration opposing it, hoping that the people from all walks of life will rise up together, so that the citizens of the concession will not be subject to the company's unreasonable demands. This is very fortunate. This is the declaration.

French Consul Gao Suo Met Yesterday Regarding the Jinliyuan Case 100

The French Consul stated that if a bank guarantee is provided first, he can mediate with the priest to initiate arbitration.

Gao Suo, the arbitrator for the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company in the Jinliyuan Wharf case, visited French Consul General Gangelin yesterday morning to discuss arbitration procedures. The reporter of the New Voice News Agency has learned the details and will report them as follows:

Gao and Gangelin Meet: Lawyer Gao Suo visited French Consul General Gangelin yesterday morning at 11:00 AM. Consul Gangelin stated that the French Concession Court had already made a judgment in the case, and that he had assumed the role of mediator due to diplomatic relations, so the French Concession Court had extended the execution of the cancellation of the contract by one month. He said that he was very pleased that Lawyer Gao had taken on the role of arbitrator. Mr. Gao then described to the French Consul the meeting he had with French arbitrator Mr. Yamina the day before, and explained that the case was now being resolved through arbitration rather than legal means, and that the French Concession Court had already made a judgment on the case. Lawyer Gao believed that it was a mistake for Mr. Yamina to request that an opinion be submitted to the French Concession Court. Consul Gangelin continued, saying that no matter what, it was not necessary to submit an opinion in writing to the French Concession Court. The first condition was that there be no unpaid rent and that there be a reliable bank guarantee. He requested that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company quickly provide the name of the guarantor bank, the amount of capital, the name of the bank president, and the address of the bank, and the person authorized to sign the payment, so that he could notify the three priests to mediate first, and then set a date for arbitration. Lawyer Gao found the French Consul's attitude to be sincere and took his leave.

Bank Guarantee: After leaving the French Consulate, Lawyer Gao visited Cai Pei, the acting Director-General of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, to explain the French Consul's opinion. Director-General Cai immediately instructed Shen Zhong-yi, the acting head of the accounting department of the bureau, to handle the bank payment. However, because yesterday was Saturday and today is Sunday, the banks are closed, so it will only be possible to complete the matter tomorrow (Monday).

The French Opinion Has Not Arrived: French arbitrator Yamina was originally scheduled to send the opinion to the French Concession Court to Lawyer Gao today, but as of last night, it had not been delivered, perhaps because the translation had not been completed yesterday.

Requesting Exemption from Tolls and Taxes on Rice Shipments Along the Way 102

Submitted for Approval by the Executive Yuan: Gospel for the Future of People's Food

The Shanghai Food Committee previously believed that regulating the people's food supply should start from all aspects. Therefore, members of the committee investigated the tolls and taxes on rice shipments arriving in Shanghai. It was found that the regular tax for each stone of japonica and indica rice was five cents, and the tax for each stone of glutinous rice was eight cents. In addition, there were surcharges for disaster relief and education, accounting for 20% and 10% respectively. Therefore, the actual tax for each stone of japonica and indica rice was six and a half cents, and the actual tax for each stone of glutinous rice was fourteen cents. Most rice boats used bills of lading indicating 50 stones, but rice merchants paid taxes based on 80% of the actual amount loaded. However, tolls were still collected at each checkpoint, and the amount was quite large. As a result, only 30% of the fees paid by merchants went to the government. The committee believes that tolls collected at checkpoints along the way are a major obstacle to rice transportation. Each day of delay results in additional expenses. All the transportation costs, taxes, and various losses incurred by merchants are passed on to consumers, which greatly affects rice prices. Therefore, a map of tolls and taxes along the way for rice shipments to Shanghai in Jiangsu Province has been drawn. As the date for tariff reduction is approaching, tolls and taxes on rice shipments should be abolished in advance. This will not only reduce rice prices, but also eliminate obstacles along the way and allow rice boats to arrive quickly, which will greatly improve the regulation of the people's food supply. The situation has been reported to the Social Affairs Bureau for submission to the Executive Yuan for approval. It is said that the municipal government has reported the situation to the Executive Yuan for consideration.

Municipal Workers' Union Petitioned 105

Nine Representatives Were Sent to the Municipal Party Headquarters. The Meeting with Committees Wu and Chen Was Very Successful.

The Municipal Workers' Union was alarmed by rumors that the Central Government intended to abolish the workers' union, so it jointly submitted a petition to the Municipal Party Headquarters and sent nine representatives, including Hu Shouqi from the Calligraphy and Fan Workers' Union, Sang Yutang from the Pharmaceutical Industry Workers' Union, Zhu Xiaoyun from the Silk and Cloth Dyeing Industry Workers' Union, Hu Xiaoxiang from the Dried Goods Workers' Union, Zhao Zhaohui from the Pharmaceutical Industry Workers' Union, Weng Ruifu from the Sauce Industry Workers' Union, Yu Yaoqiu from the Taikang Workers' Union, Yang Chunfang from the Pudong Electric Workers' Union, and Cai Xiaohe from the Tea Workers' Union, to the Municipal Party Headquarters yesterday morning at 11:00 AM with a joint petition from all municipal workers' unions. Minister Wu Kaixian and Committee Chen Junyi received them. Committees Wu and Chen reported that the municipal party had already understood the hardships and circumstances of the workers and had already made recommendations to the Central Government. They had also raised the issue at the National Civil Training Conference convened by the Central Government, but the Central Government also recognized the need for workers' unions to exist and was considering appropriate measures. The Central Government believed that it was necessary for workers' unions to exist and was considering appropriate measures. The Central Committee immediately responded to the representatives' petition to the Municipal Party headquarters and forwarded it to the Central Committee. At the same time, the headquarters issued an order to the various workers' unions to dispel any doubts. As for forwarding the request to the municipal government to order the Social Affairs Bureau to accept and mediate labor disputes, it was immediately conveyed and more appropriate measures were being considered to ensure that workers had appropriate protection. The representatives were satisfied and left. The original drafts of their two petitions are as follows:

Petition 1: Regarding the request to forward a petition to the Central Government to confirm the organization of workers' unions in order to protect workers and the overall people's movement. It has been found that the Central Government recently promulgated the Law of Industrial and Commercial Guilds, the reason for which is that in order to develop commerce, it is necessary to realize labor-capital cooperation, and in order to realize labor-capital cooperation, workers must join the industrial and commercial guilds, and then they can be integrated and jointly seek the development of business. The Central Government has made great efforts to maintain the commerce of the country and eliminate the prejudices of labor and capital, for the sake of its own interests and for the sake of the future of commerce and labor, and it is compelled to speak out. I dare to express the interests and harms and respectfully present them to your committee. It is found that people have absolute freedom to assemble and associate. All those who earn a price with physical labor and mental labor to maintain their lives are workers. This is the last teaching of the Prime Minister and should be regarded as a guideline. The organization of workers' unions is in line with the doctrine and meets the requirements of the times and the environment. Moreover, the workers' union has never been behind in the revolutionary history. They all belong to the masses and belong to the same banner. Workers and merchants can organize groups. Why not workers alone? Even if it is said that employees over the age of fifteen can send representatives to participate in the guild, what about employees under the age of fifteen? Moreover, it is still a question whether the representatives they send can implement their claims in the guild. Judging from the feelings between labor and capital on weekdays, it is undoubtedly that the workers' representatives will be suppressed by the capitalists' representatives. In this way, it goes without saying that the workers' representatives have a false name but no actual power. Unfortunately, the workers feel that their status is not guaranteed, or they may jump out and follow the reactionary heresy, which would be harmful to An Ning. It is not a big deal. The facilities of the subordinate associations should be based on conforming to the doctrine and meeting the needs of the times. The subordinate associations have always taken the realization of labor-capital cooperation and the development of commerce as their premise. They only use the capitalist's deep-rooted feudal ideas, so they use revolutionary means to promote reflection. The means are different, but the destination is the same. If the organization of workers' unions is abolished, tens of thousands of workers will be wandering in the wrong direction and will not know what to do. The gains and losses are clear, and the subordinate associations cannot remain silent. I ask your committee to understand the feelings of the people and should forward the petition to the Central Government to allow the confirmation of the organization of workers' unions, so that all the workers in Shanghai can be properly protected, and labor-capital disputes can be supervised by the party headquarters and decided by the government, and there will be no out-of-control actions, which will be beneficial to labor-capital mutual assistance, commercial development, and social safety.

Petition 2: The petition requests approval to consult the Municipal Government to order the Social Affairs Bureau to accept and handle labor disputes involving workers' unions. The organization of workers' unions is a legal group guided by the Party Headquarters and registered with the government. However, recently, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau refused to accept the Shanghai Sauce Industry Workers' Union's request for mediation of labor-capital disputes. The Social Affairs Bureau's document No. 9344 is recorded as a report proposing to modify the conditions. Please review the contents of the petition. It is clear that when disputes occur between shop assistants and employers, the Judicial Yuan has interpreted that the Labor Dispute Resolution Law does not apply. Most of the members of the union are shop assistants. The part of the requested modification of the conditions has been reported to the Municipal Government for review and instructions. It has been ordered that the parties concerned can directly appeal to the court, etc. The affiliated associations feel that the Bureau's refusal to accept the dispute of the Sauce Industry Workers' Union is equivalent to depriving the workers' rights and losing their status of the workers under the jurisdiction of the city's workers' union, and placing the workers who use the same labor and mental effort to exchange for their price outside the exception. Now, for the sake of protecting the interests of the workers and for the sake of social safety, the affiliated associations jointly submit a petition requesting your committee to consult the Municipal Government to order the Social Affairs Bureau to accept and handle the petitions of the workers' unions in the future, which is a benefit to both the Party and the government. The petition is from the Shanghai Calligraphy Workers' Union, Taikang Food Company Workers' Union, Silk Factory Industry Joint Preparatory Committee, Shanghai Grain Exchange Workers' Union, Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Cloth Industry Workers' Union, Pharmaceutical Industry Workers' Union, New Swire Warehouse Workers' Union, Pudong Electric Workers' Union, Steamship China Merchants Bureau Workers' Union, Su Ning Tea and Food Workers' Union, Porcelain Industry Workers' Union, Dried Goods Industry Workers' Union, Umbrella Workers' Union, Hui Guan Workers' Union, Silk Factory Industry Hudong District Workers' Union, Incense Industry Workers' Union, Silk Art Industry Workers' Union, Rice and Grain Workers' Union, China Food Company Workers' Union, Pollen Industry Workers' Union, Commercial Press Workers' Union, Pharmaceutical Industry Workers' Union, Jianbang Sugar and Grain Workers' Union, Shoe Industry Workers' Union, Yihe Weaving Factory Workers' Union, Silk and Cloth Dyeing Industry Workers' Union, Tea Workers' Union, Wine Industry Workers' Union, Pawn Industry Workers' Union.

The Labor Side Requests Assistance and Calls for Boycott of Japanese Goods: Declaration of the Factory Labor Adjustment Committee

Yesterday, the Ri Hua Cotton Mill Labor Adjustment Committee in Pudong issued a letter to the people of the country, saying: All fellow countrymen know that Japanese imperialists are fierce and brutal, and we do not need to introduce them again. I think everyone has long understood. This time, all of our workers in the Ri Hua Cotton Mill could not withstand the pressure of high rice prices and high salaries, and raised three universally recognized minimum requirements to the factory. Of course, the only way we can deal with this lack of awareness is to strike permanently. Even if we starve to death, we will not resume work. The reason why we want to strike and the reason why we want to strike permanently is not because we want to strike for fun, but because we have no choice but to take this last road. However, we know that the hearts of Japanese imperialists are not the same as ours, so we have long expected that this incident will be difficult to resolve satisfactorily in the shortest possible time. Therefore, we want to issue such a declaration today. Our purpose is to hope that the fellow countrymen of the country will agree to our following requirements: (1) Give us financial or written assistance. (2) We hope that no Japanese goods will be sold during our strike. Only in this way can our strike be resolved satisfactorily in the shortest possible time. Previously, the Municipal Business Rectification Association stated that the Shanghai Sand Boat Customs Declaration Association and the Wusong Customs Declaration Association were both engaged in tax reporting, and their nature was completely the same. In accordance with the principle of the Industrial and Commercial Guild Law that only one association is allowed in one area, it ordered both parties to merge and reorganize into the Shanghai Tax Reporting Industry Guild, and also appointed a rectification committee member. Later, the two parties believed that the industry to which they belonged was located in the Nanshi of Shanghai and the other was in Wusong. Although they were in the same urban area, the distance was relatively far, so disputes arose due to different claims on the location of the association. They were repeatedly convened and mediated by the former Business Rectification Association and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, but they were not resolved. The rectification committee members also delayed in taking office, resulting in the association's inability to proceed with its affairs. Yesterday, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce convened both parties again. After many explanations from Luo Qinghua, the representative of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, they each swore to take office and immediately appointed Zhu Chubaizhu Shishi Ge Zhendong and Zhou Xingshan as standing committee members to actively organize and plan to complete the organization within ten days.
